Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Economy")\]  
See also: [Economy of Dhaka](/wiki/Economy_of_Dhaka "Economy of Dhaka")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Drone_view_from_Kamal_Ataturk_Avenue.jpg/220px-Drone_view_from_Kamal_Ataturk_Avenue.jpg)](/wiki/File:Drone_view_from_Kamal_Ataturk_Avenue.jpg) Office blocks on Kemal Atatürk Avenue

As the most densely industrialized region of the country, the Greater Dhaka Area accounts for 35% of [Bangladesh's economy](/wiki/Economy_of_Bangladesh "Economy of Bangladesh").^[\[35\]](#cite_note-Rezaul_Karim-35)^ The [Globalization and World Cities Research Network](/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network "Globalization and World Cities Research Network") ranks Dhaka as a [gamma+ global city](/wiki/Global_city "Global city"), in other words, one that is instrumental in linking their region into the world economy.^[\[34\]](#cite_note-:8-34)^ Major industrial areas are [Tejgaon](/wiki/Tejgaon_Thana "Tejgaon Thana"), [Shyampur](/wiki/Shyampur_Thana "Shyampur Thana") and [Hazaribagh](/wiki/Hazaribagh_Thana "Hazaribagh Thana").^[\[150\]](#cite_note-150)^ The city has a growing middle class, driving the market for modern consumer and luxury goods.^[\[43\]](#cite_note-banglapedia-43)^^[\[151\]](#cite_note-CiE-151)^ Shopping malls serve as vital elements in the city's economy. The city has historically attracted numerous migrant workers.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-EDemo1-152)^ [Hawkers](/wiki/Hawker_centre "Hawker centre"), peddlers, small shops, [rickshaw](/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw "Cycle rickshaw") transport, roadside vendors and stalls employ a large segment of the population^[\[152\]](#cite_note-EDemo1-152)^^[\[153\]](#cite_note-Rick-153)^ -- rickshaw drivers alone number as many as 400,000.^[\[154\]](#cite_note-154)^ Half the workforce is employed in household and unorganized labour, while about 800,000 work in the textile industry. The unemployment rate in Dhaka was 23% in 2013.^[\[155\]](#cite_note-155)^{#cite_ref-155}

Almost all large local conglomerates have their corporate offices located in Dhaka. [Microcredit](/wiki/Microcredit "Microcredit") also began here and the offices of the Nobel Prize-winning [Grameen Bank](/wiki/Grameen_Bank "Grameen Bank")^[\[156\]](#cite_note-156)^ and [BRAC](/wiki/BRAC_(organization) "BRAC (organization)") (the largest [non-governmental development organization](/wiki/Non-governmental_organisation "Non-governmental organisation") in the world) are based in Dhaka.^[\[157\]](#cite_note-157)^ Urban developments have sparked a widespread construction boom; new high-rise buildings and [skyscrapers](/wiki/Skyscraper "Skyscraper") have changed the city's landscape.^[\[151\]](#cite_note-CiE-151)^ Growth has been especially strong in the finance, banking, manufacturing, telecommunications, and service sectors, while tourism, hotels, and restaurants continue as important elements of the Dhaka economy.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-EDemo1-152)^{#cite_ref-EDemo1_152-2}

Dhaka has rising traffic congestion and inadequate infrastructure; the national government has recently implemented a policy for rapid urbanization of surrounding areas and beyond by the introduction of a ten-year relief on [income tax](/wiki/Income_tax "Income tax") for new construction of facilities and buildings outside Dhaka.^[\[158\]](#cite_note-townplan-158)^{#cite_ref-townplan_158-0}  

### CBDs {#CBDs}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: CBDs")\]

The Dhaka metropolitan area boasts of several [central business districts](/wiki/Central_business_district "Central business district") (CBDs). In the southern part of the city, the riverfront of [Old Dhaka](/wiki/Old_Dhaka "Old Dhaka") is home to many small businesses, factories, and trading companies. Near Old Dhaka lies [Motijheel](/wiki/Motijheel_Thana "Motijheel Thana"), which is the biggest CBD in Bangladesh. The Motijheel area developed in the 1960s. [Motijheel](/wiki/Motijheel_Thana "Motijheel Thana") is home to the [Bangladesh Bank](/wiki/Bangladesh_Bank "Bangladesh Bank"), the nation's central bank; as well as the headquarters of the largest state-owned banks, including [Janata Bank](/wiki/Janata_Bank "Janata Bank"), [Pubali Bank](/wiki/Pubali_Bank "Pubali Bank"), [Sonali Bank](/wiki/Sonali_Bank "Sonali Bank") and [Rupali Bank](/wiki/Rupali_Bank "Rupali Bank"). By the 1990s, the affluent residential neighbourhoods of [Gulshan](/wiki/Gulshan_Thana "Gulshan Thana"), [Banani](/wiki/Banani_(town) "Banani (town)") and [Uttara](/wiki/Uttara_Thana "Uttara Thana") in the northern part of the city became a major business centre and now hosts many international companies operating in Bangladesh. The [Purbachal New Town Project](/wiki/Purbachal_New_Town_Project "Purbachal New Town Project") is planned as the city's future CBD.

The following is a list of the main CBDs in Dhaka.

* [Motijheel](/wiki/Motijheel_Thana "Motijheel Thana")
* [Kawran Bazar](/wiki/Kawran_Bazar "Kawran Bazar")
* [Paltan](/wiki/Paltan "Paltan")
* [Dhanmondi](/wiki/Dhanmondi "Dhanmondi")
* [Gulshan](/wiki/Gulshan_Thana "Gulshan Thana")
* [Banani](/wiki/Banani_(town) "Banani (town)")/[DOHS](/wiki/Banani_DOHS "Banani DOHS")
* [Uttara](/wiki/Uttara_Thana "Uttara Thana")
* [Mirpur](/wiki/Mirpur_Model_Thana "Mirpur Model Thana")/[DOHS](/wiki/Mirpur_DOHS "Mirpur DOHS")
* [Bashundhara Residential Area](/wiki/Bashundhara_Residential_Area "Bashundhara Residential Area")
* [Panthapath](/wiki/Panthapath "Panthapath")
* [Maghbazar](/wiki/Maghbazar "Maghbazar")
* [Mohakhali](/wiki/Mohakhali "Mohakhali")/[DOHS](/wiki/Mohakhali_DOHS "Mohakhali DOHS")
* [Gulistan](/wiki/Gulistan,_Dhaka "Gulistan, Dhaka")
* [Jatrabari](/wiki/Jatrabari_Thana "Jatrabari Thana")

* [Old Dhaka](/wiki/Old_Dhaka "Old Dhaka")

### Trade associations {#Trade_associations}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Trade associations")\]

Major trade associations based in the city include:

* [Federation of Bangladesh Chambers of Commerce \& Industries](/wiki/Federation_of_Bangladesh_Chambers_of_Commerce_%26_Industries "Federation of Bangladesh Chambers of Commerce & Industries") (FBCCI)
* [Dhaka Chamber of Commerce \& Industry](/wiki/Dhaka_Chamber_of_Commerce_%26_Industry "Dhaka Chamber of Commerce & Industry") (DCCI)
* [Metropolitan Chamber of Commerce and Industry](/wiki/Metropolitan_Chamber_of_Commerce_and_Industry,_Dhaka "Metropolitan Chamber of Commerce and Industry, Dhaka") (MCCI)
* [Bangladesh Garment Manufacturers and Exporters Association](/wiki/Bangladesh_Garment_Manufacturers_and_Exporters_Association "Bangladesh Garment Manufacturers and Exporters Association") (BGMEA)
* [Bangladesh Knitwear Manufacturers and Exporters Association](/wiki/Bangladesh_Knitwear_Manufacturers_and_Exporters_Association "Bangladesh Knitwear Manufacturers and Exporters Association") (BKMEA)
* [Newspaper Owners' Association of Bangladesh](/wiki/Newspaper_Owners%27_Association_of_Bangladesh "Newspaper Owners' Association of Bangladesh") (NOAB)
* [Real Estate and Housing Association of Bangladesh](/wiki/Real_Estate_and_Housing_Association_of_Bangladesh "Real Estate and Housing Association of Bangladesh") (REHAB)

### Stock market {#Stock_market}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Stock market")\]

The [Dhaka Stock Exchange](/wiki/Dhaka_Stock_Exchange "Dhaka Stock Exchange") (DSE) had a [market capitalization](/wiki/Market_capitalization "Market capitalization") of BDT 5,136,979.000 million in 2021.^[\[159\]](#cite_note-159)^ Some of the largest companies listed on the DSE include:^[\[160\]](#cite_note-160)^{#cite_ref-160}

* [Grameenphone](/wiki/Grameenphone "Grameenphone")
* [BEXIMCO](/wiki/BEXIMCO "BEXIMCO")
* [BSRM](/wiki/BSRM "BSRM")
* [Titas Gas](/wiki/Titas_Gas "Titas Gas")
* [Summit Group](/wiki/Summit_Group "Summit Group")
* [The City Bank](/wiki/The_City_Bank "The City Bank")
* [BRAC Bank](/wiki/BRAC_Bank "BRAC Bank")
* [IDLC Finance Limited](/wiki/IDLC_Finance_Limited "IDLC Finance Limited")
* [Square Pharmaceuticals](/wiki/Square_Pharmaceuticals "Square Pharmaceuticals")
* [Eastern Bank Limited](/wiki/Eastern_Bank_Ltd_(Bangladesh) "Eastern Bank Ltd (Bangladesh)")

### Population {#Population}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Population")\]

The city, in combination with localities forming the wider metropolitan area, is home to over 22 million as of 2022^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit)^.^[\[162\]](#cite_note-city_population-162)^ The population is growing by an estimated 3.3% per year,^[\[162\]](#cite_note-city_population-162)^ one of the highest rates among Asian cities.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-EDemo1-152)^ The continuing growth reflects ongoing migration from rural areas to the Dhaka urban region, which accounted for 60% of the city's growth in the 1960s and 1970s. More recently, the city's population has also grown with the expansion of city boundaries, a process that added more than a million people to the city in the 1980s.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-EDemo1-152)^ According to the *[Far Eastern Economic Review](/wiki/Far_Eastern_Economic_Review "Far Eastern Economic Review")* , Dhaka will be home to 25 million people by the end of 2025.^[\[163\]](#cite_note-163)^{#cite_ref-163}

This rapid population growth makes it difficult for the city government to provide the necessary infrastructure in a timely manner, e.g. for water supply, electricity and waste management.^[\[119\]](#cite_note-:1-119)^{#cite_ref-:1_119-5}  

#### Slums {#Slums}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Slums")\]  
See also: [Squatting in Bangladesh](/wiki/Squatting_in_Bangladesh "Squatting in Bangladesh")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Karail03.jpg/220px-Karail03.jpg)](/wiki/File:Karail03.jpg) The Karail slum in [Mohakhali](/wiki/Mohakhali "Mohakhali")

About 30% of Dhaka's population lives in [slums](/wiki/Slum "Slum") (or unplanned urban settlements), as of 2016.^[\[119\]](#cite_note-:1-119)^ Estimates from 2011 and 2015 found that there are about "3 to 5 thousand slums and squatter settlements scattered all over the city".^[\[119\]](#cite_note-:1-119)^ It is often the new arrivals, people [migrating from rural areas](/wiki/Rural-urban_migration "Rural-urban migration"), who end up living in slums. People only have very limited access to water, [sanitation](/wiki/Sanitation "Sanitation") and other services in those slum areas.{#cite_ref-:1_119-7}

Slums may be found in the outskirts and in less-visible areas such as alleyways.^[\[164\]](#cite_note-Gruebner_Sachs_Nockert_Frings_pp._1–7-164)^ As of 2021, the largest slum is in [Kamrangirchar](/wiki/Kamrangirchar_Thana "Kamrangirchar Thana"), where about 600,000 people live in slum conditions.^[\[135\]](#cite_note-:2-135)^{#cite_ref-:2_135-7}  

### Ethnicity {#Ethnicity}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Ethnicity")\]

The city population is composed of people from virtually every region of Bangladesh. The long-standing inhabitants of the old city are known as Dhakaite and have a distinctive Bengali dialect and culture. Dhaka is also home to a large number of [Bihari refugees](/wiki/Stranded_Pakistanis_in_Bangladesh "Stranded Pakistanis in Bangladesh"), who are descendants of migrant [Muslims](/wiki/Muslims "Muslims") from eastern India during 1947 and settled down in East Pakistan. The correct population of [Biharis](/wiki/Biharis "Biharis") living in the city is ambiguous, but it is estimated that there are at least 300,000 Urdu-speakers in all of Bangladesh, mostly residing in old Dhaka and in refugee camps in Dhaka, although official figures estimate only 40,000.^[\[165\]](#cite_note-fe-165)^^[\[166\]](#cite_note-dw-166)^^[\[167\]](#cite_note-ju-167)^ Between 15,000 and 20,000 of the [Rohingya](/wiki/Rohingya_people "Rohingya people"), [Santal](/wiki/Santals "Santals"), [Khasi](/wiki/Khasi_people "Khasi people"), [Garo](/wiki/Garo_(tribe) "Garo (tribe)"), [Chakma](/wiki/Chakma_people "Chakma people") and [Mandi](/wiki/Mandi_State "Mandi State") tribal peoples reside in the city.^[\[168\]](#cite_note-168)^{#cite_ref-168}  

### Language {#Language}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Language")\]  
‹ The [template](/wiki/Help:Template "Help:Template") *[Pie chart](/wiki/Template:Pie_chart "Template:Pie chart")* is being [considered for merging](/wiki/Wikipedia:Templates_for_discussion/Log/2025_January_30#Template:Pie_chart "Wikipedia:Templates for discussion/Log/2025 January 30"). ›  
Language in Dhaka (2011)  
[Bengali](/wiki/Bengali_language "Bengali language") (98%)  
[Urdu](/wiki/Urdu "Urdu") (1%)  
Others (1%)

Most residents of Dhaka speak [Bengali](/wiki/Bengali_language "Bengali language"), the national language. Other than Standard Bengali which is used in business and education, most prominent [Bengali dialects](/wiki/Bengali_dialects "Bengali dialects") spoken in the city include an *Urban East Bengal Colloquial* dialect,^[\[169\]](#cite_note-169)^ and [Dhakaiya Kutti](/wiki/Dhakaiya_Kutti "Dhakaiya Kutti") spoken in Old Dhaka.^[\[170\]](#cite_note-170)^ [English](/wiki/Bangladeshi_English "Bangladeshi English") is spoken by a large segment of the population, especially for business purposes. The city has both Bengali and English newspapers. [Urdu](/wiki/Urdu "Urdu"), including [Dhakaiya Urdu](/wiki/Dhakaiya_Urdu "Dhakaiya Urdu"), is spoken by members of several non-Bengali communities, including the [Biharis](/wiki/Bihari_people "Bihari people").^[\[171\]](#cite_note-171)^{#cite_ref-171}  

### Literacy {#Literacy}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Literacy")\]

The literacy rate in Dhaka is also increasing quickly. It was estimated at 69.2% in 2001. The literacy rate had gone up to 74.6% by 2011^[\[16\]](#cite_note-District_Statistics_2011,_Dhaka-16)^ which is significantly higher than the national average of 72%.^[\[172\]](#cite_note-bangladesh1-172)^{#cite_ref-bangladesh1_172-0}  

### Religion {#Religion}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Religion")\]  
{#cite_ref-census2011_173-0}

| Religion in Dhaka City (2011)^[\[173\]](#cite_note-census2011-173)^ |||||
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Religion ||   | Percent ||
| [Islam](/wiki/Islam_in_Bangladesh "Islam in Bangladesh") ||   | 95.72% ||
| [Hinduism](/wiki/Hinduism_in_Bangladesh "Hinduism in Bangladesh") ||   | 3.60% ||
| [Christianity](/wiki/Christianity_in_Bangladesh "Christianity in Bangladesh") ||   | 0.55% ||
| Other or not stated ||   | 0.13% ||

[Islam](/wiki/Islam_in_Bangladesh "Islam in Bangladesh") is the dominant religion of the city, with 19.3 million of the city's population being Muslim, and a majority belonging to the [Sunni](/wiki/Sunni "Sunni") sect. There is also a small [Shia](/wiki/Shia "Shia") sect, and an [Ahmadiya](/wiki/Ahmadi "Ahmadi") community. [Hinduism](/wiki/Hinduism_in_Bangladesh "Hinduism in Bangladesh") is the second-largest religion numbering around 1.47 million adherents. Smaller segments represent 1% and practise [Christianity](/wiki/Christianity_in_Bangladesh "Christianity in Bangladesh") and [Buddhism](/wiki/Buddhism_in_Bangladesh "Buddhism in Bangladesh"). In the city proper, over 8.5 million of the 8.9 million residents are Muslims, while 320,000 are Hindu and nearly 50,000 Christian.^[\[174\]](#cite_note-Dhaka_-_Banglapedia-174)^^[\[173\]](#cite_note-census2011-173)^{#cite_ref-census2011_173-1}

Infrastructure {#Infrastructure}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Infrastructure")\]  

### Transport {#Transport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Transport")\]  
Main article: [Transport in Dhaka](/wiki/Transport_in_Dhaka "Transport in Dhaka")

Motorcycles comprised half of Dhaka's registered vehicles in 2023,^[\[187\]](#cite_note-:9-188)^ while car ownership rate is only six per cent.^[\[188\]](#cite_note-:4-189)^ One of the world's least motorized cities,^[\[189\]](#cite_note-190)^ the three-wheeled [cycle rickshaw](/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw "Cycle rickshaw") is the most popular and ubiquitous mode of transport, which accounted for 54 per cent of vehicle trips in 2011.^[\[190\]](#cite_note-191)^ Dhaka is among the most congested cities in the world, and traffic was estimated to cost the local economy US$6.5 billion per year in 2020.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-liaquat2022-192)^ The average speed of a car travelling in the city is less than 7 kilometres per hour (4.3 mph).^[\[192\]](#cite_note-bird2018-193)^ [Auto rickshaws](/wiki/Auto_rickshaw "Auto rickshaw") powered by [compressed natural gas](/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas "Compressed natural gas"), often referred to by locals as "CNGs", are also a popular mode of transport.^[\[193\]](#cite_note-:15-194)^{#cite_ref-:15_194-0}  

#### Road {#Road}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Road")\]  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Rickshaws_Dhaka.jpg/167px-Rickshaws_Dhaka.jpg)](/wiki/File:Rickshaws_Dhaka.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Kazi_Nazrul_Islam_Ave_Road%2C_Dhaka._.jpg/167px-Kazi_Nazrul_Islam_Ave_Road%2C_Dhaka._.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kazi_Nazrul_Islam_Ave_Road,_Dhaka._.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Trust_taxi_Toyota_Axio%2C_Bangladesh._%2831932338632%29.jpg/177px-Trust_taxi_Toyota_Axio%2C_Bangladesh._%2831932338632%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Trust_taxi_Toyota_Axio,_Bangladesh._(31932338632).jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Mirpur-banani_flyover.JPG/157px-Mirpur-banani_flyover.JPG)](/wiki/File:Mirpur-banani_flyover.JPG)  
Clockwise from top-left: heavy rickshaw traffic in Dhaka, congested main road, Mirpur-Banani flyover and Dhaka yellow taxi.

The city is connected to other parts of the country through highway and railway links. Five of Bangladesh's eight major [national highways](/wiki/List_of_roads_in_Bangladesh#Roads_and_highways "List of roads in Bangladesh") start from the city: [N1](/wiki/N1_(Bangladesh) "N1 (Bangladesh)"), [N2](/wiki/N2_(Bangladesh) "N2 (Bangladesh)"), [N3](/wiki/N3_(Bangladesh) "N3 (Bangladesh)"), [N5](/wiki/N5_(Bangladesh) "N5 (Bangladesh)") and [N8](/wiki/N8_(Bangladesh) "N8 (Bangladesh)"). Dhaka is also directly connected to the two longest routes of the [Asian Highway Network](/wiki/Asian_Highway_Network "Asian Highway Network"): [AH1](/wiki/AH1 "AH1") and [AH2](/wiki/AH2 "AH2"), as well as to the [AH41](/wiki/AH41 "AH41") route. Highway links to the Indian cities of [Kolkata](/wiki/Kolkata "Kolkata"), [Agartala](/wiki/Agartala "Agartala"), [Guwahati](/wiki/Guwahati "Guwahati") and [Shillong](/wiki/Shillong "Shillong") have been established by the BRTC and private bus companies, which also run regular international bus services to those cities from Dhaka.^[\[194\]](#cite_note-BRTC-195)^^[\[195\]](#cite_note-196)^{#cite_ref-196}

The [Dhaka Elevated Expressway](/wiki/Dhaka_Elevated_Expressway "Dhaka Elevated Expressway"), the first of its kind in the country, improves connectivity between the northern part of the city and the central, southern, and south-eastern parts.^[\[196\]](#cite_note-:13-197)^ An extension, the [Dhaka--Ashulia Elevated Expressway](/wiki/Dhaka%E2%80%93Ashulia_Elevated_Expressway "Dhaka–Ashulia Elevated Expressway"), is expected to open in 2026.^[\[197\]](#cite_note-198)^{#cite_ref-198}  

#### Rickshaws {#Rickshaws}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Rickshaws")\]

[Cycle rickshaws](/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw "Cycle rickshaw") and CNG [auto-rickshaws](/wiki/Auto_rickshaw#Bangladesh "Auto rickshaw") are the main modes of transport within the metro area, with more than 1.5 million rickshaws running each day:^[\[198\]](#cite_note-:23-199)^ the highest number in any city in the world.^[\[199\]](#cite_note-200)^ However, only around 220 thousand rickshaws are licensed by the city government.^[\[198\]](#cite_note-:23-199)^ Over 15,000 legally registered CNGs serve passengers in Dhaka, with thousands more operating illegally.^[\[200\]](#cite_note-201)^{#cite_ref-201}  

#### Ride sharing {#Ride_sharing}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Ride sharing")\]

Since 2016, [Uber](/wiki/Uber "Uber") and [Pathao](/wiki/Pathao "Pathao") have dominated the ride-sharing market in Dhaka, which offer both car and motorcycle services.^[\[201\]](#cite_note-f452-202)^^[\[202\]](#cite_note-203)^ Ride-sharing services have led to a decline in the use of CNG auto-rickshaws,^[\[203\]](#cite_note-204)^ although Uber has expanded its services to include CNG auto-rickshaws in 2021.^[\[204\]](#cite_note-205)^{#cite_ref-205}  

#### Bus {#Bus}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Bus")\]

Buses carried about 1.9 million passengers per day in 2007.^[\[205\]](#cite_note-206)^ Public buses in Dhaka are primarily operated by numerous private companies, with a minority run by the state-owned [Bangladesh Road Transport Corporation](/wiki/Bangladesh_Road_Transport_Corporation "Bangladesh Road Transport Corporation") (BRTC).^[\[206\]](#cite_note-207)^ [BRTC](/wiki/Bangladesh_Road_Transport_Corporation "Bangladesh Road Transport Corporation") buses are red, based initially on the [Routemaster](/wiki/AEC_Routemaster "AEC Routemaster") buses of London. There are three inter-district bus terminals in Dhaka, which are located in the city's [Mohakhali](/wiki/Mohakhali "Mohakhali"), Saidabad, and Gabtoli areas. It is now planned to move three inter-district bus terminals outside the town.^[\[207\]](#cite_note-208)^ Highway links to the Indian cities of [Kolkata](/wiki/Kolkata "Kolkata"), [Agartala](/wiki/Agartala "Agartala"), [Guwahati](/wiki/Guwahati "Guwahati") and [Shillong](/wiki/Shillong "Shillong") have been established by the BRTC and private bus companies, which also run regular international bus services to those cities from Dhaka.^[\[194\]](#cite_note-BRTC-195)^{#cite_ref-BRTC_195-1}

Set to open in December 2024, the 20.5-kilometre (12.7 mi) [Dhaka Bus Rapid Transit](/wiki/Dhaka_BRT "Dhaka BRT") system is expected to reduce travel time from Dhaka to the [satellite town](/wiki/Satellite_town "Satellite town") of [Gazipur](/wiki/Gazipur "Gazipur") from as long as four hours to just 35--40 minutes.^[\[208\]](#cite_note-t839-209)^{#cite_ref-t839_209-0}  

#### Waterways {#Waterways}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Waterways")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/%E0%A6%AC%E0%A7%81%E0%A6%A1%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%97%E0%A6%99%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%97%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A7%A9.jpg/220px-%E0%A6%AC%E0%A7%81%E0%A6%A1%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%97%E0%A6%99%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%97%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A7%A9.jpg)](/wiki/File:%E0%A6%AC%E0%A7%81%E0%A6%A1%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%97%E0%A6%99%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%97%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A7%A9.jpg) Some boats and launches on the river Buriganga.

The [Sadarghat River Port](/wiki/Dhaka_Sadarghat "Dhaka Sadarghat") on the banks of the [Buriganga River](/wiki/Buriganga_River "Buriganga River") serves for the transport of goods and passengers upriver and to other ports in Bangladesh.^[\[209\]](#cite_note-210)^ Inter-city and inter-district motor vessels and passenger ferry services are used by many people to travel riverine regions of the country from the city. [Water bus](/wiki/Water_taxi "Water taxi") services are available on the Buriganga River and [Hatirjheel](/wiki/Hatirjheel_Thana "Hatirjheel Thana") and Gulshan lakes, providing connectivity via two routes, [Tejgaon](/wiki/Tejgaon_Thana "Tejgaon Thana")--[Gulshan](/wiki/Gulshan_Thana "Gulshan Thana") and Tejgaon--[Rampura](/wiki/Rampura_Thana "Rampura Thana").^[\[210\]](#cite_note-211)^{#cite_ref-211}  

#### Rail {#Rail}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Rail")\]  
Further information: [Dhaka Metro Rail](/wiki/Dhaka_Metro_Rail "Dhaka Metro Rail") and [Dhaka Circular Railway](/wiki/Dhaka_Circular_Railway "Dhaka Circular Railway")  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Bangladesh_Railway%2C_Komlapur_Railway_Station.jpg/200px-Bangladesh_Railway%2C_Komlapur_Railway_Station.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bangladesh_Railway,_Komlapur_Railway_Station.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Agargaon_metro_station_Platform_10.jpg/200px-Agargaon_metro_station_Platform_10.jpg)](/wiki/File:Agargaon_metro_station_Platform_10.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/18Metro_at_Agargaon_metro_station_Platform.jpg/200px-18Metro_at_Agargaon_metro_station_Platform.jpg)](/wiki/File:18Metro_at_Agargaon_metro_station_Platform.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Interior_of_Uttara_North_09.jpg/200px-Interior_of_Uttara_North_09.jpg)](/wiki/File:Interior_of_Uttara_North_09.jpg)  
Clockwise from top-left: [DEMU Train](/wiki/Diesel_multiple_unit "Diesel multiple unit") at [Kamalapur Railway Station](/wiki/Kamalapur_railway_station "Kamalapur railway station"), [Metro Rail station](/wiki/Dhaka_Metro_Rail "Dhaka Metro Rail") sign in [Agargaon](/wiki/Agargaon "Agargaon"), [Metro train](/wiki/Dhaka_Metro_Rail "Dhaka Metro Rail") interior and exterior.

[Kamalapur railway station](/wiki/Kamalapur_railway_station "Kamalapur railway station"), situated on the northeast side of [Motijheel](/wiki/Motijheel "Motijheel"), is the largest and busiest of the city's railway stations.^[\[211\]](#cite_note-Morshed-212)^ It was designed by American architect [Robert Boughey](/wiki/Robert_Boughey "Robert Boughey") and was completed in 1969.^[\[212\]](#cite_note-213)^ The state-owned [Bangladesh Railway](/wiki/Bangladesh_Railway "Bangladesh Railway") provides suburban and national services, with regular express train services connecting Dhaka with other major urban areas, such as [Chittagong](/wiki/Chittagong "Chittagong"), [Rajshahi](/wiki/Rajshahi "Rajshahi"), [Khulna](/wiki/Khulna "Khulna"), [Sylhet](/wiki/Sylhet "Sylhet") and [Rangpur](/wiki/Rangpur_City "Rangpur City").^[\[213\]](#cite_note-214)^ The [Maitree Express](/wiki/Maitree_Express "Maitree Express") and the [Mitali Express](/wiki/Mitali_Express "Mitali Express") provides connections from Dhaka to [West Bengal](/wiki/West_Bengal "West Bengal") in India.^[\[214\]](#cite_note-215)^^[\[215\]](#cite_note-:26-216)^{#cite_ref-:26_216-0}

Dhaka Metro Rail is a [mass rapid transit](/wiki/Rapid_transit "Rapid transit") system serving Dhaka, [Bangladesh](/wiki/Bangladesh "Bangladesh"). It is a part of the 20-year-long Strategic Transport Plan (STP) outlined by the [Dhaka Transport Coordination Authority (DTCA)](/wiki/Dhaka_Transport_Coordination_Authority "Dhaka Transport Coordination Authority").^[\[216\]](#cite_note-:0-217)^ The first phase of Dhaka Metro's [MRT Line 6](/wiki/MRT_Line_6 "MRT Line 6") was inaugurated by [Prime Minister](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bangladesh "Prime Minister of Bangladesh") [Sheikh Hasina](/wiki/Sheikh_Hasina "Sheikh Hasina") and commenced commercial operations on 28 December 2022.^[\[217\]](#cite_note-218)^^[\[218\]](#cite_note-219)^{#cite_ref-219}

The metro network is planned to contain six lines. Before the opening of the Dhaka Metro Rail, Dhaka was the biggest city in the world without a mass rapid transit system.^[\[219\]](#cite_note-220)^ Unrelated to the metro, there is also a proposal to build a [subway](/wiki/Dhaka_Subway "Dhaka Subway")^[\[220\]](#cite_note-221)^ and an [orbital railway system](/wiki/Dhaka_Circular_Railway "Dhaka Circular Railway").^[\[221\]](#cite_note-a604-222)^{#cite_ref-a604_222-0}  

#### Air {#Air}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Air")\]  
See also: [Hazrat Shahjalal International Airport](/wiki/Hazrat_Shahjalal_International_Airport "Hazrat Shahjalal International Airport")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Biman_Bangladesh_Airlines_-_S2-AJV_-_The_Gaangchil_-_Boeing_787-8_Dreamliner_-_40125_-_HSIA.jpg/220px-Biman_Bangladesh_Airlines_-_S2-AJV_-_The_Gaangchil_-_Boeing_787-8_Dreamliner_-_40125_-_HSIA.jpg)](/wiki/File:Biman_Bangladesh_Airlines_-_S2-AJV_-_The_Gaangchil_-_Boeing_787-8_Dreamliner_-_40125_-_HSIA.jpg) Biman Bangladesh in Hazrat Shahjalal International Airport

[Hazrat Shahjalal International Airport](/wiki/Shahjalal_International_Airport "Shahjalal International Airport") (formerly Zia International Airport),^[\[222\]](#cite_note-223)^ located 15 kilometres (9.3 mi) north of Dhaka city centre, is the largest and busiest international airport in the country.^[\[223\]](#cite_note-Air-224)^ Although built with an annual passenger-handling capacity of 8 million,^[\[224\]](#cite_note-capacity-225)^ it handled more than 11 million passengers in 2023.^[\[225\]](#cite_note-226)^ The average aircraft movement per day is around 330 flights.^[\[226\]](#cite_note-:132-227)^ It is the hub of most [Bangladeshi airlines](/wiki/List_of_airlines_of_Bangladesh "List of airlines of Bangladesh"). Domestic service flies to [Chittagong](/wiki/Shah_Amanat_International_Airport "Shah Amanat International Airport"), [Sylhet](/wiki/Osmani_International_Airport "Osmani International Airport"), [Rajshahi](/wiki/Shah_Makhdum_Airport "Shah Makhdum Airport"), [Cox's Bazar](/wiki/Cox%27s_Bazar_Airport "Cox's Bazar Airport"), [Jessore](/wiki/Jessore_Airport "Jessore Airport"), [Barisal](/wiki/Barisal_Airport "Barisal Airport"), and [Saidpur](/wiki/Saidpur_Airport "Saidpur Airport") ([Rangpur](/wiki/Rangpur_District "Rangpur District")), and international services fly to major cities in Asia, Europe and the Middle East.^[\[227\]](#cite_note-intsched-228)^^[\[228\]](#cite_note-dhkcityguide-229)^ The airport's capacity is expected to more than double to 20 million once the modern [third terminal](/wiki/Hazrat_Shahjalal_International_Airport#Terminal_3 "Hazrat Shahjalal International Airport") opens fully in October 2024.^[\[229\]](#cite_note-230)^^\[*[needs update](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")*\]^ According to the project design, the third terminal will have 12 boarding bridges and 16 conveyor belts. The terminal will have 115 check-in counters and 128 immigration desks.^[\[230\]](#cite_note-q379-231)^{#cite_ref-q379_231-0}  

### Water supply and sanitation {#Water_supply_and_sanitation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Water supply and sanitation")\]  
See also: [Water supply and sanitation in Bangladesh](/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Bangladesh "Water supply and sanitation in Bangladesh") and [Water management in Dhaka](/wiki/Water_management_in_Dhaka "Water management in Dhaka")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Night_view_of_Hatirjheel.jpg/220px-Night_view_of_Hatirjheel.jpg)](/wiki/File:Night_view_of_Hatirjheel.jpg) [Hatirjheel](/wiki/Hatirjheel "Hatirjheel") Lake is a key water reservoir in Dhaka. Its lakefront was transformed from a slum area into a bypass under an [urban renewal](/wiki/Urban_renewal "Urban renewal") project

[Water management in Dhaka](/wiki/Water_management_in_Dhaka "Water management in Dhaka") faces numerous challenges such as [flooding](/wiki/Flood "Flood"), poor service quality, [groundwater depletion](/wiki/Overdrafting "Overdrafting"), inadequate [sanitation](/wiki/Sanitation "Sanitation"), [polluted river water](/wiki/Water_pollution "Water pollution"), unplanned urban development, and the existence of large [slums](/wiki/Slum "Slum").^[\[231\]](#cite_note-:3-232)^{#cite_ref-:3_232-0}

The [Dhaka Water Supply and Sewerage Authority](/wiki/Dhaka_Water_Supply_and_Sewerage_Authority "Dhaka Water Supply and Sewerage Authority") (Dhaka WASA) is "responsible for providing drinking water, sewerage, and storm-water drainage services to the city".^[\[119\]](#cite_note-:1-119)^ The work of Dhaka WASA is funded by the [Ministry of Local Government, Rural Development, and Cooperatives](/wiki/Ministry_of_Local_Government,_Rural_Development_and_Co-operatives "Ministry of Local Government, Rural Development and Co-operatives").{#cite_ref-:1_119-8}

87% of the city's growing water demand is sourced from [groundwater](/wiki/Groundwater "Groundwater") (as of 2021). This is because the extreme contamination of rivers and lakes makes surface water treatment economically and technologically unfeasible.^[\[135\]](#cite_note-:2-135)^ While around 20% of the daily demand of 2.4 billion litres of water is met with surface water from five [treatment plants](/wiki/Treatment_plant "Treatment plant"),^[\[232\]](#cite_note-:7-233)^ the groundwater table is falling at a rate of two to three metres per year.^[\[231\]](#cite_note-:3-232)^^[\[232\]](#cite_note-:7-233)^{#cite_ref-:7_233-1}

The Bangladesh Urban Informal Settlements Survey 2016 included a representative sample of 588 households across small, medium and large [slums](/wiki/Slum "Slum") in Dhaka. It showed that 68% of the households accessed [piped water](/wiki/Piped_water "Piped water") through a shared connection within the slum compound. The poorest households shared a waterpoint with 43 other households on average compared to 23 sharers among the richest households. In terms of [sanitation](/wiki/Sanitation "Sanitation"), only 8% of the slum households had access to a [flush toilet](/wiki/Flush_toilet "Flush toilet") connected to a [septic tank](/wiki/Septic_tank "Septic tank"), while 78% used improved [pit latrines](/wiki/Pit_latrine "Pit latrine") and the remaining 10% depended on hanging latrines.^[\[135\]](#cite_note-:2-135)^{#cite_ref-:2_135-9}  

### Sewage treatment plants {#Sewage_treatment_plants}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Sewage treatment plants")\]

The [sewage system](/wiki/Sewerage "Sewerage") is inadequate, with 70 per cent of the two million cubic metres of [sewage](/wiki/Sewage "Sewage") produced daily being discharged into rivers, according to wastewater management experts.^[\[233\]](#cite_note-:5-234)^ Due to improper maintenance and the age of the system, the majority of the sewerage network is out of operation.^[\[234\]](#cite_note-s372-235)^^[\[235\]](#cite_note-o611-236)^ Most buildings handle their own sewage by constructing [soak pits](/wiki/Soak_pit "Soak pit") or [septic tanks](/wiki/Septic_tank "Septic tank"), often connected to [storm drains](/wiki/Storm_drain "Storm drain"). Consequently, 80 per cent of [faecal sludge](/wiki/Faecal_sludge "Faecal sludge") ends up in rivers, according to experts.^[\[233\]](#cite_note-:5-234)^{#cite_ref-:5_234-1}

Dhaka is served by two [sewage treatment plants](/wiki/Sewage_treatment_plants "Sewage treatment plants").^[\[236\]](#cite_note-237)^ The Pagla Sewerage Treatment Plant (PSTP) in [Narayanganj District](/wiki/Narayanganj_District "Narayanganj District") has a capacity of 120 [megalitres](/wiki/Megalitres "Megalitres") per day^[\[119\]](#cite_note-:1-119)^ but can only utilise one-third of its capacity,^[\[233\]](#cite_note-:5-234)^ handling just 10 per cent of the city's waste.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-o611-236)^ The Dasherkandi Sewage Treatment Plant, opened in 2023, is South Asia's largest, with a capacity to treat 500 megalitres, or 20--25% of the city's 2,000 megalitres of sewage generated daily.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-:6-238)^ However, it is also hampered by a lack of sewage connections.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-o611-236)^{#cite_ref-o611_236-2}

The [Bangladesh Government](/wiki/Government_of_Bangladesh "Government of Bangladesh") and the Dhaka Water Supply and Sewerage Authority (DWASA) are implementing an ambitious plan, called *Dhaka Sewerage Master Plan* , to treat most of the residential and industrial wastewater through the construction of several sewage treatment plants. The Bangladesh Government is planning to install over 12 large new sewage treatment plants over the next 20 years.^[\[124\]](#cite_note-:02-124)^{#cite_ref-:02_124-3}  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Culture")\]  
Main article: [Culture of Dhaka](/wiki/Culture_of_Dhaka "Culture of Dhaka")  

### Literature {#Literature}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Literature")\]

Dhaka is a major centre for [Bengali literature](/wiki/Bengali_literature "Bengali literature"). It has been the hub of [Bengali Muslim](/wiki/Bengali_Muslim "Bengali Muslim") literature for more than a century. Its heritage also includes historic [Urdu](/wiki/Urdu "Urdu") and [Persian](/wiki/Persian_language "Persian language") literary traditions. *Dark Diamond* by [Shazia Omar](/wiki/Shazia_Omar "Shazia Omar") in set in Mughal-era Dhaka during the reign of [Shaista Khan](/wiki/Shaista_Khan "Shaista Khan"), the Mughal viceroy and uncle of Emperor Aurangzeb.^[\[238\]](#cite_note-239)^*The Soldier in the Attic* by [Akhteruzzaman Elias](/wiki/Akhteruzzaman_Elias "Akhteruzzaman Elias") is considered to be one of the best depictions of life in [Old Dhaka](/wiki/Old_Dhaka "Old Dhaka") and is set during Bengali uprisings in 1969. *[A Golden Age](/wiki/A_Golden_Age "A Golden Age")* by [Tahmima Anam](/wiki/Tahmima_Anam "Tahmima Anam") is also set in Dhaka during the Bangladeshi War of Independence and includes references to the [Dhaka Club](/wiki/Dhaka_Club "Dhaka Club"), the [Dhaka University](/wiki/Dhaka_University "Dhaka University") and the [Dhanmondi](/wiki/Dhanmondi "Dhanmondi") area.{#cite_ref-239}  

### Textiles {#Textiles}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Textiles")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Dhaka_Sari_Fabric_1.jpg/220px-Dhaka_Sari_Fabric_1.jpg)](/wiki/File:Dhaka_Sari_Fabric_1.jpg) Indigenous [sari](/wiki/Sari "Sari") fabrics, including [Jamdani](/wiki/Jamdani "Jamdani"), at a store in Dhaka

For centuries, the region around Dhaka has been the centre of production for fine cotton textiles. [Muslin](/wiki/Muslin "Muslin") was abundantly produced in the region. The weavers of Dhaka were patronized by the rulers of Bengal and Delhi. They supplied textiles to the Mughal imperial court. The city of Dhaka became one of the most important centres of the cotton textile trade in the 17th century. It was literally the capital of the [Muslin trade in Bengal](/wiki/Muslin_trade_in_Bengal "Muslin trade in Bengal"). Merchants from around the world came to Dhaka to buy its much sought after cotton fabrics. [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") has recognized [Jamdani](/wiki/Jamdani "Jamdani") muslin as an [intangible cultural heritage](/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage "Intangible cultural heritage").^[\[239\]](#cite_note-240)^ According to UNESCO, "Jamdani is a vividly patterned, sheer cotton fabric, traditionally woven on a handloom by craftspeople and apprentices around Dhaka".^[\[240\]](#cite_note-unesco_00879-241)^ UNESCO believes "the Jamdani sari is a symbol of identity, dignity and self-recognition and provides wearers with a sense of cultural identity and social cohesion. The weavers develop an occupational identity and take great pride in their heritage; they enjoy social recognition and are highly respected for their skills".^[\[240\]](#cite_note-unesco_00879-241)^{#cite_ref-unesco_00879_241-1}  

### Festivals {#Festivals}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Festivals")\]  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Shaheed_Minar.JPG/197px-Shaheed_Minar.JPG)](/wiki/File:Shaheed_Minar.JPG)  
The [Central Shaheed Minar](/wiki/Shaheed_Minar,_Dhaka "Shaheed Minar, Dhaka") on [Language Movement Day](/wiki/Language_Movement_Day "Language Movement Day")  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg/187px-Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg)  
Dhaka's annual [Mangal Shobhajatra](/wiki/Mangal_Shobhajatra "Mangal Shobhajatra") during the [Bengali New Year](/wiki/Bengali_New_Year "Bengali New Year") is recognized by [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") as an [intangible cultural heritage](/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage "Intangible cultural heritage") of humanity

Annual celebrations for [Language Martyrs' Day](/wiki/Language_Movement_Day "Language Movement Day") (21 February), [Independence Day](/wiki/Bangladeshi_Independence_Day "Bangladeshi Independence Day") (26 March), and [Victory Day](/wiki/Victory_Day_(Bangladesh) "Victory Day (Bangladesh)") (16 December) are prominently celebrated across the city. Dhaka's people congregate at the [Shaheed Minar](/wiki/Shaheed_Minar,_Dhaka "Shaheed Minar, Dhaka") and the [Jatiyo Smriti Soudho](/wiki/Jatiyo_Smriti_Soudho "Jatiyo Smriti Soudho") to remember the national heroes of the liberation war. These occasions are observed with public ceremonies and rallies on public grounds. Many schools and colleges organize fairs, festivals, and concerts in which citizens from all levels of society participate.^[\[241\]](#cite_note-Cul-242)^*[Pohela Baishakh](/wiki/Pohela_Baishakh "Pohela Baishakh")* , the Bengali New Year, falls annually on 14 April and is popularly celebrated across the city.^[\[241\]](#cite_note-Cul-242)^ Large crowds of people gather on the streets of [Shahbag](/wiki/Shahbag "Shahbag"), [Ramna Park](/wiki/Ramna_Park "Ramna Park") and the campus of the University of Dhaka for celebrations. *[Pahela Falgun](/wiki/Pahela_Falgun "Pahela Falgun")* , the first day of spring of the month [Falgun](/wiki/Falgun "Falgun") in the [Bengali calendar](/wiki/Bengali_calendar "Bengali calendar"), is also festively celebrated in the city.^[\[242\]](#cite_note-history-243)^ This day is marked with colourful celebration and traditionally, women wear yellow saris to celebrate this day. This celebration is also known as *Basanta Utsab* (Spring Festival). [Nabanna](/wiki/Nabanna "Nabanna") is a harvest celebration, usually celebrated with food and dance, and music on the 1st day of the month of Agrahayan of the Bengali year. Birthdays of Rabindranath Tagore and Kazi Nazrul Islam are observed respectively as [Rabindra Jayanti](/wiki/Rabindra_Jayanti "Rabindra Jayanti") and [Nazrul Jayanti](/wiki/Nazrul_Jayanti "Nazrul Jayanti"). The [Ekushey Book Fair](/wiki/Ekushey_Book_Fair "Ekushey Book Fair"), which is arranged each year by [Bangla Academy](/wiki/Bangla_Academy "Bangla Academy"), takes place for the whole month of February. This event is dedicated to the martyrs who died on 21 February 1952 in a demonstration calling for the establishment of Bengali as one of the state languages of former [East Pakistan](/wiki/Historical_regions_of_Pakistan "Historical regions of Pakistan"). [Shakrain Festival](/wiki/Shakrain "Shakrain") is an annual celebration observed with the flying of kites.^[\[243\]](#cite_note-dstar-244)^ It is usually observed in the old part of the city at the end of Poush, the ninth month of the Bengali calendar (14 or 15 January in the [Gregorian calendar](/wiki/Gregorian_calendar "Gregorian calendar")).{#cite_ref-dstar_244-0}  

#### Religious Festivals {#Religious_Festivals}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: Religious Festivals")\]

The Islamic festivals of [Eid ul-Fitr](/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr "Eid ul-Fitr"), [Eid ul-Adha](/wiki/Eid_ul-Adha "Eid ul-Adha"), [Eid-E-Miladunnabi](/wiki/Mawlid "Mawlid") and [Muharram](/wiki/Muharram "Muharram"); the Hindu festival of [Durga Puja](/wiki/Durga_Puja "Durga Puja"); the Buddhist festival of [Buddha Purnima](/wiki/Buddha_Purnima "Buddha Purnima"); and the [Christian festival of Christmas](/wiki/Christmas "Christmas") witness widespread celebrations across the city.  

### Music {#Music}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=50 "Edit section: Music")\]

The popularity of music groups and rock bands such as [Warfaze](/wiki/Warfaze "Warfaze"), [Shironamhin](/wiki/Shironamhin "Shironamhin"), [Artcell](/wiki/Artcell "Artcell") and other solo artists such as Aryan Chowdhary, [Ayub Bachchu](/wiki/Ayub_Bachchu "Ayub Bachchu"), and [Shafin Ahmed](/wiki/Shafin_Ahmed "Shafin Ahmed") is growing day by day among the newer generations of Dhaka.^[\[244\]](#cite_note-245)^ Despite this, traditional [folk music](/wiki/Music_of_Bangladesh "Music of Bangladesh") remains widely popular.^[\[245\]](#cite_note-246)^ The works of the national poet [Kazi Nazrul Islam](/wiki/Kazi_Nazrul_Islam "Kazi Nazrul Islam"), national anthem writer [Rabindranath Tagore](/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore "Rabindranath Tagore") and mystic saint songwriter [Lalon](/wiki/Lalon "Lalon") have a widespread following across Dhaka.^[\[246\]](#cite_note-247)^ Bailey Road is known as *natak para* (drama neighbourhood) for its two theatre halls.^[\[247\]](#cite_note-248)^{#cite_ref-248}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Grave_-_Kazi_Nazrul_Islam_-_University_of_Dhaka_Campus_-_Dhaka_2015-05-31_2306-2307.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Grave_-_Kazi_Nazrul_Islam_-_University_of_Dhaka_Campus_-_Dhaka_2015-05-31_2306-2307.tif.jpg)](/wiki/File:Grave_-_Kazi_Nazrul_Islam_-_University_of_Dhaka_Campus_-_Dhaka_2015-05-31_2306-2307.tif) [Mausoleum of Kazi Nazrul Islam](/wiki/Mausoleum_of_Kazi_Nazrul_Islam "Mausoleum of Kazi Nazrul Islam") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ekushey_Book_Fair_2018_%2824%29.jpg/220px-Ekushey_Book_Fair_2018_%2824%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ekushey_Book_Fair_2018_(24).jpg) A Bengali book stall at the [Ekushey Book Fair](/wiki/Ekushey_Book_Fair "Ekushey Book Fair")

### Rickshaws {#Rickshaws_2}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: Rickshaws")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rickshaw_back_decoration.jpg/170px-Rickshaw_back_decoration.jpg)](/wiki/File:Rickshaw_back_decoration.jpg) Rickshaw art

[Rickshaws](/wiki/Rickshaws_in_Bangladesh "Rickshaws in Bangladesh") have become a symbol of the city. Rickshaws are colourfully painted with floral patterns and depictions of birds, animals, movie stars, religious text, historical events and national heroes. According to [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO"), "Rickshaws and rickshaw painting are viewed as a key part of the city's cultural tradition and a dynamic form of urban folk art".^[\[39\]](#cite_note-unesco_01589-39)^{#cite_ref-unesco_01589_39-1}  

### Cuisine {#Cuisine}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=54 "Edit section: Cuisine")\]  
See also: [Biryani](/wiki/Biryani "Biryani") and [Bangladeshi cuisine](/wiki/Bangladeshi_cuisine "Bangladeshi cuisine")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Basmati_Kacchi_Biryani_%282%29.jpg/220px-Basmati_Kacchi_Biryani_%282%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Basmati_Kacchi_Biryani_(2).jpg) Dhaka has a renowned style of mutton (goat meat) and potato [biryani](/wiki/Biryani "Biryani"), known as the *Kacchi Biryani*. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Bakorkhani.jpg/220px-Bakorkhani.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bakorkhani.jpg) [Bakarkhani](/wiki/Bakarkhani "Bakarkhani") is a snake item mostly eaten in [old Dhaka](/wiki/Old_Dhaka "Old Dhaka")

Historically, Dhaka has been the culinary capital of Bengal for Muslim cuisine, particularly [Mughlai cuisine](/wiki/Mughlai_cuisine "Mughlai cuisine"). Restaurants in the city serve several types of [biryani](/wiki/Biryani "Biryani"), including Kacchi Biryani ([goat meat](/wiki/Goat_meat "Goat meat")), [Tehari](/wiki/Tehri_(dish) "Tehri (dish)") ([beef](/wiki/Beef "Beef")), Murag Pulao ([chicken](/wiki/Chicken "Chicken")), and Ilish Pulao ([ilish](/wiki/Ilish "Ilish") fish). [Khichuri rice](/wiki/Khichuri "Khichuri") is a popular [comfort food](/wiki/Comfort_food "Comfort food"). A distinct variant of Bengali-Mughlai cuisine evolved in the city. Like other Mughal cities, a special tradition exists to eat [nihari](/wiki/Nihari "Nihari") beef stew during breakfast. In Dhaka, the nihari stew can be eaten with Bengali breads.^[\[248\]](#cite_note-249)^ Chefs from Dhaka, the former Mughal provincial capital, served in the kitchens of the Nawabs of Dhaka and Murshidabad. They invented the *Kacchi Biryani* , which is a variant of [biryani](/wiki/Biryani "Biryani") with mutton steaks and potatoes. One of the longest surviving outlets serving authentic *Kacchi Biryani* is Fakhruddin's.^[\[249\]](#cite_note-250)^ *Kacchi Biryani* is highly popular in Bangladeshi cuisine, with food critic and former [MasterChef Australia](/wiki/MasterChef_Australia "MasterChef Australia") judge [Matt Preston](/wiki/Matt_Preston "Matt Preston") praising its use of potatoes.^[\[250\]](#cite_note-251)^ [Borhani](/wiki/Borhani "Borhani") is served as a drink alongside biryani. The Nawabi cuisine of Dhaka was notable for its *patishapta* dessert and the *Kubali [pulao](/wiki/Pilaf "Pilaf")* . The [korma](/wiki/Korma "Korma") recipe of the Nawab family was included by [Madhur Jaffrey](/wiki/Madhur_Jaffrey "Madhur Jaffrey") in her cookbook "Madhur Jaffrey's Ultimate Curry Bible".^[\[251\]](#cite_note-252)^ [Bakarkhani](/wiki/Bakarkhani "Bakarkhani") breads from Dhaka were served in the courts of Mughal rulers.^[\[252\]](#cite_note-253)^{#cite_ref-253}

Since 1939, [Haji biryani](/wiki/Haji_biryani "Haji biryani") has been a leading biryani restaurant in the city. Dhaka also has a style of *Murag Pulao* (chicken biryani) which uses [turmeric](/wiki/Turmeric "Turmeric") and *[malai](/wiki/Malai "Malai")* (cream of milk) together.^[\[253\]](#cite_note-254)^ Local [kebabs](/wiki/Kebab "Kebab") are widely eaten when dining out. The [seekh kebab](/wiki/Seekh_kebab "Seekh kebab") and [chicken tikka](/wiki/Chicken_tikka "Chicken tikka") are the most popular dishes in kebab restaurants, which are eaten with either [naan](/wiki/Naan "Naan") or [paratha](/wiki/Paratha "Paratha"). [Liver](/wiki/Liver_(food) "Liver (food)") is often eaten with breads, as a stuffing, or as a curry. [Star Kabab](/wiki/Star_Kabab "Star Kabab") is the most popular kebab chain in the city, alongside other chains and gourmet restaurants.^[\[254\]](#cite_note-255)^ Different kinds of [bhurta](/wiki/Bhurta "Bhurta"), which refers to mashed vegetables, are widely eaten. Various types of Bengali fish curry are found in the city. Along with [South Asian cuisine](/wiki/South_Asian_cuisine "South Asian cuisine"), a large variety of Western and [Chinese cuisine](/wiki/Chinese_cuisine "Chinese cuisine") is served at numerous restaurants and food courts.^[\[151\]](#cite_note-CiE-151)^ Upmarket areas include many Thai, Japanese and Korean restaurants.^[\[255\]](#cite_note-256)^ [Italian](/wiki/Italian_cuisine "Italian cuisine") food is also very popular in Dhaka, especially in upmarket areas.^[\[256\]](#cite_note-257)^{#cite_ref-257}

During [Ramadan](/wiki/Ramadan "Ramadan"), [Chowkbazaar](/wiki/Chowkbazar_Thana "Chowkbazar Thana") becomes a busy marketplace for *[iftar](/wiki/Iftar "Iftar")* items. The *[jilapi](/wiki/Jalebi "Jalebi")* of Dhaka are much thicker than counterparts in India and Pakistan.^[\[257\]](#cite_note-258)^ The [Shahi jilapi](/wiki/Shahi_jilapi "Shahi jilapi") (king's jilapi) is one of the thickest jilapi produced. The *[phuchka](/wiki/Panipuri "Panipuri")* and *[jhalmuri](/wiki/Jhalmuri "Jhalmuri")* are popular street food. Dhaka hosts an array of Bengali dessert chains that sell a wide variety of [sweets](/wiki/List_of_Bangladeshi_sweets_and_desserts "List of Bangladeshi sweets and desserts"). [Samosas](/wiki/Samosa "Samosa") and *shingaras* are also widely eaten traditional snacks. In recent years, the number of Bangladeshi-owned [burger](/wiki/Hamburger "Hamburger") outlets has increased across the city. Notable bakeries include the [Prince of Wales bakery](/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_bakery "Prince of Wales bakery") in Old Dhaka and the [Cooper's](/wiki/Cooper%27s_(bakery) "Cooper's (bakery)") chain.{#cite_ref-258}  

### Architecture {#Architecture}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=55 "Edit section: Architecture")\]  
See also: [List of tallest buildings in Dhaka](/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Dhaka "List of tallest buildings in Dhaka") and [Architecture of Dhaka](/wiki/Architecture_of_Dhaka "Architecture of Dhaka")  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Haturia_House_-_Khanka_E_Aliya_-_Dhaka_by_NKS.jpg/200px-Haturia_House_-_Khanka_E_Aliya_-_Dhaka_by_NKS.jpg)](/wiki/File:Haturia_House_-_Khanka_E_Aliya_-_Dhaka_by_NKS.jpg)  
Haturia House was built in the Anglo-Mughal style in 1920  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Gulshan_Society_Jame_Masjid_04.jpg/200px-Gulshan_Society_Jame_Masjid_04.jpg)](/wiki/File:Gulshan_Society_Jame_Masjid_04.jpg)  
[Gulshan Society Mosque](/wiki/Gulshan_Society_Mosque "Gulshan Society Mosque") was built in the modernist style in 2017

The architectural history of Dhaka can be subdivided into the Mughal, British, and modern periods. As a result, Dhaka has landmarks of [Mughal architecture](/wiki/Mughal_architecture "Mughal architecture"), [Indo-Saracenic architecture](/wiki/Indo-Saracenic_architecture "Indo-Saracenic architecture"), and [modernist architecture](/wiki/Modernist_architecture "Modernist architecture"). The oldest brick structure in the city is the [Binat Bibi Mosque](/wiki/Binat_Bibi_Mosque "Binat Bibi Mosque"), which was built in 1454 in the [Narinda](/wiki/Narinda "Narinda") area of Dhaka during the reign of the Sultan [Nasiruddin Mahmud Shah](/wiki/Mahmud_Shah_(Sultan_of_Bengal) "Mahmud Shah (Sultan of Bengal)") (r. 1435 -- 1459) of the Bengal Sultanate.^[\[258\]](#cite_note-259)^^[\[259\]](#cite_note-260)^ Old Dhaka is home to over 2000 buildings built between the 16th and 19th centuries, which form an integral part of Dhaka's cultural heritage. Modern Dhaka is often criticized as a concrete jungle.^[\[260\]](#cite_note-261)^{#cite_ref-261}

In the old part of the city, the fading grandeur of the Mughal era is evident in the crumbling, neglected caravanserai like [Bara Katra](/wiki/Bara_Katra "Bara Katra") and [Choto Katra](/wiki/Chhota_Katra "Chhota Katra"). Some structures like the [Nimtali arch](/wiki/Nimtali_arch "Nimtali arch") have been restored. The old city features narrow alleyways with high-walled lanes and houses with indoor courtyards.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-himalmag1-74)^ The early 20th century government quarter in [Ramna](/wiki/Ramna "Ramna") includes stately colonial buildings set amidst gardens and parks.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-himalmag1-74)^ Among colonial buildings, the [Curzon Hall](/wiki/Curzon_Hall "Curzon Hall") stands out for "synthesizing imperial grandiosity with sporadic Mughal motifs".^[\[261\]](#cite_note-25Buildings-262)^{#cite_ref-25Buildings_262-0}

Amongst modernist buildings, the [Grameenphone](/wiki/Grameenphone "Grameenphone") headquarters is described as "a paradigm setter for corporate Bangladesh".^[\[261\]](#cite_note-25Buildings-262)^ The Museum of Independence and its attached national monument were inspired by the "land-water mysticism of deltaic Bengal" and the "evocative expansiveness of a Roman forum or the geographical assemblage of an Egyptian *mastaba* sanctuary".^[\[261\]](#cite_note-25Buildings-262)^ Dhaka's Art Institute, designed by [Muzharul Islam](/wiki/Muzharul_Islam "Muzharul Islam"), was the pioneering building of Bengali regional modernism.^[\[261\]](#cite_note-25Buildings-262)^ The vast expanse of the national parliament complex was designed by [Louis Kahn](/wiki/Louis_Kahn "Louis Kahn"). It is celebrated as Dhaka's pre-eminent civic space.^[\[262\]](#cite_note-263)^ The national parliament complex comprises 200 acres (800,000 m^2^) in the heart of the city.^[\[263\]](#cite_note-264)^ The [Kamalapur railway station](/wiki/Kamalapur_railway_station "Kamalapur railway station") was designed by American architect [Robert Boughey](/wiki/Robert_Boughey "Robert Boughey").^[\[211\]](#cite_note-Morshed-212)^ In the last few decades, Bangladesh's new wave of cultural architecture has been influenced by Bengali aesthetics and the environment.^[\[264\]](#cite_note-265)^ [City Centre Bangladesh](/wiki/City_Centre_Bangladesh "City Centre Bangladesh") is currently the tallest building in the city.{#cite_ref-265}  

### Publishing and media {#Publishing_and_media}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=56 "Edit section: Publishing and media")\]  
See also: [Mass media in Bangladesh](/wiki/Mass_media_in_Bangladesh "Mass media in Bangladesh")  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Collection_of_Bangladesh_Newspapers.jpg/192px-Collection_of_Bangladesh_Newspapers.jpg)](/wiki/File:Collection_of_Bangladesh_Newspapers.jpg)  
Major titles of the Bengali press  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Collection_of_Bangladesh_English_Newspapers.jpg/192px-Collection_of_Bangladesh_English_Newspapers.jpg)](/wiki/File:Collection_of_Bangladesh_English_Newspapers.jpg)  
Dhaka's English language newspapers

In 1849, the Katra Press became the first printing press in the city. The name alludes to the *[katra](/wiki/Katra_(Dhaka) "Katra (Dhaka)")* , the Bengali word for caravanserai. In 1856, *[Dacca News](/wiki/Dacca_News "Dacca News")* became the first English-language newspaper in the city. The Dacca News Press was the first commercial printing press in the city. Books published in Dhaka stirred discourse in the social and literary circles of Bengal. The Bengal Library Catalogue records the expansion of the publishing industry during the 1860s. Between 1877 and 1895, there were 45 printing presses in Dhaka. Between 1863 and 1900, more than a hundred Islamic [puthi](/wiki/Puthi "Puthi") were published in Dhaka. Bookshops sprang up in [Chowkbazaar](/wiki/Chowkbazar_Thana "Chowkbazar Thana"), Islampur, Mughaltuli, and Patuatuli. Albert Library was a den for left-wing activists.^[\[265\]](#cite_note-thedailystar2-266)^ After partition, the number of publishing houses in Dhaka rose from 27 in 1947 to 88 in 1966.^[\[265\]](#cite_note-thedailystar2-266)^ Prominent bookshops included Wheeler's Bookstall and Presidency Library. Banglabazaar has since become the hub of the book trade.^[\[265\]](#cite_note-thedailystar2-266)^ Bookworm is a famous local book shop that has been located adjacent to the Prime Minister's Office for three decades until being ordered to relocate in 2022;^[\[266\]](#cite_note-267)^^[\[267\]](#cite_note-268)^^[\[268\]](#cite_note-269)^ it is now located in Justice Shahabuddin Ahmed Park.^[\[269\]](#cite_note-270)^{#cite_ref-270}

Dhaka is the centre of the national media in Bangladesh. It is home to the state-owned [Bangladesh Television](/wiki/Bangladesh_Television "Bangladesh Television") and [Bangladesh Betar](/wiki/Bangladesh_Betar "Bangladesh Betar"). In recent years, the number of privately owned television channels and radio stations has increased greatly. There are over two dozen Bengali language television channels in the private sector, including 24-hour news channels. Radio is also popular across the city. Dhaka is home to national newspapers, including Bengali newspapers like *[Prothom Alo](/wiki/Prothom_Alo "Prothom Alo")* ,^[\[270\]](#cite_note-271)^ *[Ittefaq](/wiki/The_Daily_Ittefaq "The Daily Ittefaq")* , *[Inqilab](/wiki/Daily_Inqilab "Daily Inqilab")* , *[Janakantha](/wiki/Janakantha "Janakantha")* , and *[Jugantor](/wiki/Jugantor "Jugantor")* ; as well as English language newspapers *[The Daily Star](/wiki/The_Daily_Star_(Bangladesh) "The Daily Star (Bangladesh)")* ,^[\[271\]](#cite_note-272)^ *[The Financial Express](/wiki/The_Financial_Express_(Bangladesh) "The Financial Express (Bangladesh)")* , *The Business Standard* , *[Dhaka Tribune](/wiki/Dhaka_Tribune "Dhaka Tribune")* , and *[New Age](/wiki/New_Age_(Bangladesh) "New Age (Bangladesh)")* . Broadcast media based in Dhaka include [Gaan Bangla](/wiki/Gaan_Bangla "Gaan Bangla"), [Banglavision](/wiki/Banglavision "Banglavision"), [DBC News](/wiki/DBC_News "DBC News"), [Somoy TV](/wiki/Somoy_TV "Somoy TV"), [Independent TV](/wiki/Independent_Television_(Bangladesh) "Independent Television (Bangladesh)") and [Ekattor](/wiki/Ekattor "Ekattor").{#cite_ref-272}  

Education and research {#Education_and_research}
------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=57 "Edit section: Education and research")\]  
See also: [Education in Bangladesh](/wiki/Education_in_Bangladesh "Education in Bangladesh")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Curzon_Hall%2C_University_of_Dhaka_2023_department.jpg/220px-Curzon_Hall%2C_University_of_Dhaka_2023_department.jpg)](/wiki/File:Curzon_Hall,_University_of_Dhaka_2023_department.jpg) [Curzon Hall](/wiki/Curzon_Hall "Curzon Hall") is the home of the Faculty of Science, Dhaka University

Dhaka has the largest number of schools, colleges and universities of any Bangladeshi city. The education system is divided into five levels: primary (from grades 1 to 5), junior (from grades 6 to 8), secondary (from grades 9 to 10), higher secondary (from grades 11 to 12) and tertiary.^[\[272\]](#cite_note-CompEd-273)^ The five years of primary education concludes with a Primary School Completion (PSC) Examination, the three years of junior education concludes with [Junior School Certificate](/wiki/Junior_School_Certificate "Junior School Certificate") (JSC) Examination. Next, two years of secondary education concludes with a [Secondary School Certificate](/wiki/Secondary_School_Certificate "Secondary School Certificate") (SSC) Examination. Students who pass this examination proceed to two years of higher secondary or intermediate training, which culminate in a [Higher Secondary School Certificate](/wiki/Higher_Secondary_School_Certificate "Higher Secondary School Certificate") (HSC) Examination.^[\[272\]](#cite_note-CompEd-273)^ Education is mainly offered in Bengali. However, English is also widely taught and used. Many Muslim families send their children to attend part-time courses or even to pursue full-time religious education alongside other subjects, which is imparted in Bengali and Arabic in schools, colleges and [madrasas](/wiki/Madrasa#Bangladesh "Madrasa").^[\[272\]](#cite_note-CompEd-273)^{#cite_ref-CompEd_273-2}

There are [52 universities](/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Bangladesh "List of universities in Bangladesh") in Dhaka. [Dhaka College](/wiki/Dhaka_College "Dhaka College") is the oldest institution for higher education in the city and among the earliest established in British India, founded in 1841. Since independence, Dhaka has seen the establishment of numerous public and private colleges and universities that offer undergraduate and graduate degrees as well as a variety of doctoral programs.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ The [University of Dhaka](/wiki/University_of_Dhaka "University of Dhaka") is the oldest public university in the country which has more than 30,000 students and 1,800 faculty staff.^[\[273\]](#cite_note-274)^ It was established in 1921 being the first university in the region. The university has 23 research centres and 70 departments, faculties, and institutes.^[\[274\]](#cite_note-DhakaU-275)^ Eminent seats of higher education include [Bangladesh University of Engineering and Technology](/wiki/Bangladesh_University_of_Engineering_and_Technology "Bangladesh University of Engineering and Technology") (BUET), [Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujib Medical University](/wiki/Bangabandhu_Sheikh_Mujib_Medical_University "Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujib Medical University") (BSMMU), [Jagannath University](/wiki/Jagannath_University "Jagannath University") and [Sher-e-Bangla Agricultural University](/wiki/Sher-e-Bangla_Agricultural_University "Sher-e-Bangla Agricultural University").^[\[275\]](#cite_note-276)^ [Bangladesh University of Professionals](/wiki/Bangladesh_University_of_Professionals "Bangladesh University of Professionals") (BUP), situated in [Mirpur Cantonment](/wiki/Mirpur_Cantonment "Mirpur Cantonment"), is the largest public university affiliated with the armed forces.^[\[276\]](#cite_note-277)^ [Dhaka Medical College](/wiki/Dhaka_Medical_College_and_Hospital "Dhaka Medical College and Hospital") is one of the oldest and largest [medical colleges](/wiki/Medical_Colleges_of_Bangladesh "Medical Colleges of Bangladesh") in the country.^[\[277\]](#cite_note-278)^ Founded in 1875, the Dhaka Medical School was the first medical school in British East Bengal, which became [Sir Salimullah Medical College](/wiki/Sir_Salimullah_Medical_College "Sir Salimullah Medical College") in 1962.^[\[278\]](#cite_note-279)^ Other government medical colleges are [Shaheed Suhrawardy Medical College](/wiki/Shaheed_Suhrawardy_Medical_College "Shaheed Suhrawardy Medical College"), [Mugda Medical College](/wiki/Mugda_Medical_College_%26_Hospital "Mugda Medical College & Hospital") and [Armed Forces Medical College, Dhaka](/wiki/Armed_Forces_Medical_College,_Dhaka,_Bangladesh "Armed Forces Medical College, Dhaka, Bangladesh").{#cite_ref-279}

Two [Nobel laureates](/wiki/Nobel_laureate "Nobel laureate") are prominently associated with the city, including [Amartya Sen](/wiki/Amartya_Sen "Amartya Sen") who grew up in the city during the 1930s and 1940s, and attended [St. Gregory's School](/wiki/St._Gregory%27s_High_School_and_College "St. Gregory's High School and College");^[\[279\]](#cite_note-280)^^[\[280\]](#cite_note-281)^^[\[281\]](#cite_note-282)^^[\[282\]](#cite_note-283)^ and [Muhammad Yunus](/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus "Muhammad Yunus"), who studied at [Dhaka University](/wiki/Dhaka_University "Dhaka University"), founded the [Grameen Bank](/wiki/Grameen_Bank "Grameen Bank") and lives in the city.^[\[283\]](#cite_note-284)^{#cite_ref-284}  

### Learned societies and think tanks {#Learned_societies_and_think_tanks}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=58 "Edit section: Learned societies and think tanks")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg/220px-Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg) The [Bangla Academy](/wiki/Bangla_Academy "Bangla Academy")

* [Asiatic Society of Bangladesh](/wiki/Asiatic_Society_of_Bangladesh "Asiatic Society of Bangladesh")
* [Atomic Energy Centre, Dhaka](/wiki/Atomic_Energy_Centre,_Dhaka "Atomic Energy Centre, Dhaka")
* [Bangla Academy](/wiki/Bangla_Academy "Bangla Academy")
* [Bangladesh Academy of Sciences](/wiki/Bangladesh_Academy_of_Sciences "Bangladesh Academy of Sciences")
* [Bangladesh Enterprise Institute](/wiki/Bangladesh_Enterprise_Institute "Bangladesh Enterprise Institute")
* [Bangladesh Institute of Development Studies](/wiki/Bangladesh_Institute_of_Development_Studies "Bangladesh Institute of Development Studies")
* [Bangladesh Centre for Advanced Studies](/wiki/Bangladesh_Centre_for_Advanced_Studies "Bangladesh Centre for Advanced Studies")
* [Bangladesh Institute of Law and International Affairs](/wiki/Bangladesh_Institute_of_Law_and_International_Affairs "Bangladesh Institute of Law and International Affairs")
* [Bangladesh Institute of Peace \& Security Studies](/wiki/Bangladesh_Institute_of_Peace_%26_Security_Studies "Bangladesh Institute of Peace & Security Studies")
* [Centre for Policy Dialogue](/wiki/Centre_for_Policy_Dialogue "Centre for Policy Dialogue")
* [Centre on Integrated Rural Development for Asia and the Pacific](/wiki/Centre_on_Integrated_Rural_Development_for_Asia_and_the_Pacific "Centre on Integrated Rural Development for Asia and the Pacific")
* [International Centre for Diarrhoeal Disease Research, Bangladesh](/wiki/International_Centre_for_Diarrhoeal_Disease_Research,_Bangladesh "International Centre for Diarrhoeal Disease Research, Bangladesh")
* [International Jute Study Group](/wiki/International_Jute_Study_Group "International Jute Study Group")
* [Space Research and Remote Sensing Organization](/wiki/Space_Research_and_Remote_Sensing_Organization "Space Research and Remote Sensing Organization")
* [Yunus Centre](/wiki/Yunus_Centre "Yunus Centre")

Sports {#Sports}
----------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=59 "Edit section: Sports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Mirpur_Indoor_Stadium%2C_Dhaka.jpeg/220px-Mirpur_Indoor_Stadium%2C_Dhaka.jpeg)](/wiki/File:Mirpur_Indoor_Stadium,_Dhaka.jpeg) Mirpur Indoor Stadium [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/BPL_Fire_Works.jpg/220px-BPL_Fire_Works.jpg)](/wiki/File:BPL_Fire_Works.jpg) Fireworks at the launch of a [Bangladesh Premier League](/wiki/Bangladesh_Premier_League "Bangladesh Premier League") season at [Sher-e-Bangla National Cricket Stadium](/wiki/Sher-e-Bangla_National_Cricket_Stadium "Sher-e-Bangla National Cricket Stadium") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Bangabandhu_National_Stadium%2C_Dhaka%2C_Bangladesh.jpg/221px-Bangabandhu_National_Stadium%2C_Dhaka%2C_Bangladesh.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bangabandhu_National_Stadium,_Dhaka,_Bangladesh.jpg) [Bangabandhu National Stadium](/wiki/Bangabandhu_National_Stadium "Bangabandhu National Stadium"), the largest football stadium in Dhaka

[Cricket](/wiki/Cricket "Cricket") and [football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") are the two most popular sports in Dhaka and across the nation.^[\[284\]](#cite_note-285)^ Teams are fielded in intra-city and national competitions by many schools, colleges and private entities. The [Dhaka Metropolis cricket team](/wiki/Dhaka_Metropolis_cricket_team "Dhaka Metropolis cricket team") represents Dhaka City in the [National Cricket League](/wiki/National_Cricket_League "National Cricket League"), the oldest domestic [first-class cricket](/wiki/First-class_cricket "First-class cricket") competition in Bangladesh.^[\[285\]](#cite_note-286)^ The [Dhaka Premier League](/wiki/Dhaka_Premier_Division_Cricket_League "Dhaka Premier Division Cricket League") is the only domestic [List A cricket](/wiki/List_A_cricket "List A cricket") tournament now in Bangladesh. It gained List A status in [2013--14 season](/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Bangladeshi_cricket_season "2013–14 Bangladeshi cricket season").^[\[286\]](#cite_note-287)^ In domestic [Twenty20](/wiki/Twenty20 "Twenty20") cricket, Dhaka has a [Bangladesh Premier League](/wiki/Bangladesh_Premier_League "Bangladesh Premier League") franchise known as [Dhaka Capitals](/wiki/Minister_Dhaka "Minister Dhaka").^[\[287\]](#cite_note-288)^{#cite_ref-288}

Dhaka has the distinction of having hosted the first official [Test cricket](/wiki/Test_cricket "Test cricket") match of the [Pakistan cricket team](/wiki/Pakistan_cricket_team "Pakistan cricket team") in 1954 against India.^[\[288\]](#cite_note-First_test-289)^ The [Bangabandhu National Stadium](/wiki/Bangabandhu_National_Stadium "Bangabandhu National Stadium") was formerly the main venue for domestic and international cricket matches, but now exclusively hosts football matches.^[\[288\]](#cite_note-First_test-289)^ It hosted the opening ceremony of the [2011 Cricket World Cup](/wiki/2011_Cricket_World_Cup "2011 Cricket World Cup"),^[\[289\]](#cite_note-290)^ while the [Sher-e-Bangla National Cricket Stadium](/wiki/Sher-e-Bangla_National_Cricket_Stadium "Sher-e-Bangla National Cricket Stadium"), exclusively used for cricket, hosted 6 matches of the tournament including two [quarter-final](/wiki/2011_Cricket_World_Cup_knockout_stage#Quarter-finals "2011 Cricket World Cup knockout stage") matches.^[\[290\]](#cite_note-2011WC-291)^ Dhaka has also hosted the [South Asian Games](/wiki/South_Asian_Games "South Asian Games") three times, in [1985](/wiki/1985_South_Asian_Games "1985 South Asian Games"), [1993](/wiki/1993_South_Asian_Games "1993 South Asian Games") and [2010](/wiki/2010_South_Asian_Games "2010 South Asian Games"). Dhaka is the first city to host the games three times. The Bangabandhu National Stadium was the main venue for all three editions.^[\[291\]](#cite_note-news1-292)^ Dhaka also hosted the [ICC Men's T20 World Cup](/wiki/ICC_Men%27s_T20_World_Cup "ICC Men's T20 World Cup"), along with Chittagong and [Sylhet](/wiki/Sylhet "Sylhet"), in [2014](/wiki/2014_ICC_World_Twenty20 "2014 ICC World Twenty20").^[\[292\]](#cite_note-293)^{#cite_ref-293}

In football, the [Dhaka Derby](/wiki/Dhaka_Derby "Dhaka Derby") between [Mohammedan SC](/wiki/Dhaka_Mohammedan "Dhaka Mohammedan") and [Abahani Limited Dhaka](/wiki/Abahani_Limited_Dhaka "Abahani Limited Dhaka") is the biggest sports rivalry in the country. The two clubs have maintained their fierce rivalry over the years in the [Bangladesh Football Premier League](/wiki/Bangladesh_Premier_League_(football) "Bangladesh Premier League (football)") and previously in the historic [Dhaka League](/wiki/Dhaka_League "Dhaka League"), which is the second oldest football league in South Asia, officially commencing in 1948.^[\[293\]](#cite_note-starsport-294)^ The Bangabandhu National Stadium in Dhaka has been the home venue for the [national football team](/wiki/Bangladesh_national_football_team "Bangladesh national football team") since 2005.^[\[294\]](#cite_note-295)^ It has hosted the [SAFF Championship](/wiki/SAFF_Championship "SAFF Championship") on three occasions, with the first being the [2003 edition](/wiki/2003_South_Asian_Football_Federation_Gold_Cup "2003 South Asian Football Federation Gold Cup"), which Bangladesh went on to win.^[\[295\]](#cite_note-296)^ The [1978 AFC Youth Championship](/wiki/1978_AFC_Youth_Championship "1978 AFC Youth Championship") was the first major international tournament hosted by the stadium.^[\[296\]](#cite_note-297)^{#cite_ref-297}

The [National Sports Council](/wiki/National_Sports_Council "National Sports Council"), responsible for promoting sports activities across the nation, is based in Dhaka. Dhaka also has stadiums largely used for domestic events such as the [Bangladesh Army Stadium](/wiki/Bangladesh_Army_Stadium "Bangladesh Army Stadium"), the [Bir Sherestha Shaheed Shipahi Mostafa Kamal Stadium](/wiki/Bir_Sherestha_Shaheed_Shipahi_Mostafa_Kamal_Stadium "Bir Sherestha Shaheed Shipahi Mostafa Kamal Stadium"), the [Dhanmondi Cricket Stadium](/wiki/Dhanmondi_Cricket_Stadium "Dhanmondi Cricket Stadium"), the [Maulana Bhasani Hockey Stadium](/wiki/Maulana_Bhasani_Hockey_Stadium "Maulana Bhasani Hockey Stadium") and the [Outer Stadium Ground](/wiki/Outer_Stadium_Ground "Outer Stadium Ground").^[\[297\]](#cite_note-298)^ The city's colleges and universities are active in intercollegiate athletics.^[\[298\]](#cite_note-299)^{#cite_ref-299}

There are two [golf courses](/wiki/Golf_course "Golf course") in Dhaka, [Army Golf Club](/wiki/Army_Golf_Club "Army Golf Club") and [Kurmitola Golf Club](/wiki/Kurmitola_Golf_Club "Kurmitola Golf Club").^[\[299\]](#cite_note-300)^{#cite_ref-300}  

Twin towns -- sister cities {#Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities}
-----------------------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dhaka&action=edit&section=60 "Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities")\]

* [![India](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png)](/wiki/India "India") [Kolkata](/wiki/Kolkata "Kolkata"), [India](/wiki/India "India")^[\[300\]](#cite_note-301)^{#cite_ref-301}

40. **[\^](#cite_ref-britannicaetymology_40-0)** ["Dhaka"](https://www.britannica.com/place/Dhaka). *[Encyclopaedia Britannica](/wiki/Encyclopaedia_Britannica "Encyclopaedia Britannica")* . 26 June 2023. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20171010143325/https://www.britannica.com/place/Dhaka) from the original on 10 October 2017. Retrieved 11 February 2018. Dhaka's name is said to refer to the dhak tree, once common in the area, or to Dhakeshwari ("The Hidden Goddess"), whose shrine is located in the western part of the city.{#cite_note-britannicaetymology-40}
{#cite_note-britannicaetymology-40}
41. **[\^](#cite_ref-dailystaretym_41-0)** Ayan, Anindya J. (28 January 2018). ["History of Dhaka's origin"](https://www.thedailystar.net/video-stories/watch-glimpse-the-history-dhakas-origin-208639?amp). *[The Daily Star](/wiki/The_Daily_Star_(Bangladesh) "The Daily Star (Bangladesh)")* . [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20230415135035/https://www.thedailystar.net/video-stories/watch-glimpse-the-history-dhakas-origin-208639?amp) from the original on 15 April 2023. Retrieved 15 April 2023. In history, it is often believed that Raja Ballal Sen of the Sen Dynasty of Bengal founded the Dhakeshwari Temple in the 12th century to mark the place of his birth and to pay tribute to the patron goddess of this region. The name Dhaka is believed to have originated from Dhakeshwari in the same way Athens got its name from Athena, the patron goddess of the Greek city.{#cite_note-dailystaretym-41}
{#cite_note-dailystaretym-41}
